  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_28e3e5d0-f052-4f6f-8e6b-ee462ba780ce'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6803145413740867275"><b>Return to the realm of the Blood in <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i>—featuring four revelatory all-new adventures of Jaenelle and her kindred….</b><br/><br/>Jaenelle is the most powerful Witch ever known, centuries of hopes and dreams made flesh at last.   <span id="freeText6803145413740867275" style="display:none"><b>Return to the realm of the Blood in <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i>—featuring four revelatory all-new adventures of Jaenelle and her kindred….</b><br /><br />Jaenelle is the most powerful Witch ever known, centuries of hopes and dreams made flesh at last. She has forged ties with three of the realm’s mightiest Blood warriors: Saetan, the High Lord of Hell, who trains Jaenelle in magic and adopts her as his daughter; Lucivar, the winged Eyrien warlord who becomes her protector; and the near-immortal Daemon born to be Witch’s lover. Jaenelle has assumed her rightful place as Queen of the Darkness and restored order and peace to the realms…but at a terrible cost.<br /><br />In <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i>, discover the origin of the mystical Jewels, and experience the forbidden passion between Lucivar and a simple hearth witch. Witness the clash between Saetan and a Priestess that may forever change reality. And learn whether the sacrifice of Jaenelle’s magic has destroyed any hope of happiness between her and Daemon.</span>

<div id="review_2806575854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2806575854" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2806575854?book_show_action=true">Jul 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=bb-b-2019">bb-b-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=cool-creatures">cool-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with">chick-i-want-to-hang-out-with</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=witches-warlocks-and-magic">witches-warlocks-and-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=4-5-stars">4-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=romantasy">romantasy</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2806575854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15988431881441373949"><b>Overall Rating 4 Stars ★ ☆✰⭐</b><br/><br/>Dreams Made Flesh is a compilation of stories told in the world of the Black Jewels. It is four stories of various lengths and I can’t say that I usually enjoy that since you don’t get the same depth in a short story but since we have a lot of world building and knowledge of this world it works.<br/><br/>★ ☆✰ <b>Weaver of Dreams</b> is a pretty short story of how the Black Widows and Weavers were gifted their magic from one of Draka’s daughters. It is a cute story shown from the persp</span>
  <span id="freeText15988431881441373949" style="display:none"><b>Overall Rating 4 Stars ★ ☆✰⭐</b><br /><br />Dreams Made Flesh is a compilation of stories told in the world of the Black Jewels. It is four stories of various lengths and I can’t say that I usually enjoy that since you don’t get the same depth in a short story but since we have a lot of world building and knowledge of this world it works.<br /><br />★ ☆✰ <b>Weaver of Dreams</b> is a pretty short story of how the Black Widows and Weavers were gifted their magic from one of Draka’s daughters. It is a cute story shown from the perspective of a spider and that isn’t something you read every day. Because it is so short it wasn’t my favorite of the compilation.<br /><br />★ ☆✰⭐✩<b>The Prince of Ebon Rih</b> is my favorite story in this book and the main reason I’d recommend reading it. It is set before Queen of Darkness, which is great since I was so confused with Lucivar was already married in it and we’d never read anything about his wife prior to that. <br /><br />Marian comes from a family that didn’t value her because she was a hearth witch and not powerfully jeweled. After her father makes an unforgivable bargain, Marian is saved from a horrible fate and ends up in Lucivar’s household. <br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Marian sank down on one of the kitchen chairs and braced her head in her hands. He got mad at her for sweeping up spilled sugar but dragged her outside to throw a skillet at bales of hay. She threw a pot at him and missed, so he was going to teach her how to clobber him with a skillet. Even taking into account that he was an Eyrien male, there was only one explanation for his behavior. The man was insane.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br />I loved the story of how Lucivar and Marian became friendly and then more than friendly. They had plenty of things to overcome due to his power being so much greater than hers, his mother’s interference and Roxy who is a spiteful little twit. But the patience that Lucivar shows to Marian to make her his wife eventually was incredibly tender and sweet.<br /><br />So happy for his HEA love story.<br /><br />★ ☆✰⭐ <b>Zuulaman</b> explains why even though it might have been easier to kill Lucivar or Daemon, Heckatah wouldn’t dare. Saetan has been the mentor in these books. He is the quiet patient man with crazy kids and kindred running around everywhere. But once he walked in the land of the living and married the wrong woman, once she tried to play him and an entire people paid for her vicious game. This story shows that even when you thought you hated Heckatah as much as possible, you are wrong and could hate her more. Saetan is a powerful man and no one remembers Zuulaman now because of the part they played in Heckatah’s schemes.<br /><br />I liked how this story shows how vicious Saetan could be if pushed. It also showed how he was with his boys when they were young and what a good father he could have been to Daemon and Lucivar, had they not been stolen from him. The take away from Zuulaman…Don’t mess with Saetan.<br /><br />★ ☆✰⭐ <b>Kaeleer’s Heart</b> is in the aftermath of Queen of Darkness. Jaenelle has paid a price to save the blood and the land and the price was high. Only the kindred believed enough to save her. She is weak and healing and Daemon would never press her for anything, he will stand by her through it all, so why does it feel like she is pushing him away.<br /><br />I really liked how this explored how sometimes when someone has been ill, they are put in a little protective box and it is so hard to see when they are ready to be better. Jaenelle is healing and while weak she is better but the boys of the family aren’t ready to see it. With a little push from Surreal and Marrian they will try to help Jaenelle out and get her back into fighting and loving form.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15988431881441373949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/5322233-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5322233-melissa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer401955897" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2609941863611215946">From the moment I began reading the first book in Anne Bishop's Black Jewel Series I was captivated, moved, and entralled with the story and the characters. Having fallen in love with the dark jewel trilogy I was expecting a lot from this book. AND I got it... The book consists of 4 stories. Usually I am not a big fan of short stories, but "The Prince of Ebon Rih" and "Kaeleer's Heart" are long enough, and detailed enough to be really satisfying. I really liked the way the story of Lucivar and M</span>
  <span id="freeText2609941863611215946" style="display:none">From the moment I began reading the first book in Anne Bishop's Black Jewel Series I was captivated, moved, and entralled with the story and the characters. Having fallen in love with the dark jewel trilogy I was expecting a lot from this book. AND I got it... The book consists of 4 stories. Usually I am not a big fan of short stories, but "The Prince of Ebon Rih" and "Kaeleer's Heart" are long enough, and detailed enough to be really satisfying. I really liked the way the story of Lucivar and Marian was fleshed out. My only complaint is that I think it would have been even better if Lucivar had had a conversation with Marian's family...<br />I'm also so glad Anne Bishop added a footnote to the end of "The Queen of Darkness." "Kaeleer's Heart" lets the reader know how Janelle's recovery progressed and what her powers are like with twilight's dawn. It adds a feeling of completeness that I missed with "The Queen of Darkness."<br />"Zuulaman" is short, but haunting. It adds on to the story of Saetan and Heketah; it doesn't tell us much we didn't already know, but it adds emotion and depth to Saetan's character--and Hekatah's depravity.<br />I absolutely love the Dark Jewels universe and these stories. The authors style pulls your whole-heartedly into the story and envelops you in the character's world. This book of stories fills in some of missing events between the original three and makes the collection more vibrant and meaningful. An absolute must read if you like the dark jewels universe.</span>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17509333887395991673"><a href='https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-P2t_kCrvCsU/Xkip1UQk-2I/AAAAAAAAwUs/5UIkfi3-KosNJcc3AoAm1_2TA_z_gbnMwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Dreams.jpg' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img height='640' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1583196146i/29048961.jpg' width='390' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>There are four short stories in Dreams Made Flesh.</b><br/><br/>The first story, <b>Weaver of Dreams</b> features the Spider spinning her web and how and who gifted them with magic.<br/><br/>In the second one, <b>The Prince of Ebon Rih</b>, Lucivar is the main character, In this story, we learned how he met and fell in love with Marian, his wife.<br/><br/>The third one, <b>Zuulaman</b> is all about Saetan. Is narrated in the past. Saetan is still married to Hekatah and he has a son with her and another one on the way. In this one, you learn of t</span>
  <span id="freeText17509333887395991673" style="display:none"><a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-P2t_kCrvCsU/Xkip1UQk-2I/AAAAAAAAwUs/5UIkfi3-KosNJcc3AoAm1_2TA_z_gbnMwCLcBGAsYHQ/s1600/Dreams.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><b>There are four short stories in Dreams Made Flesh.</b><br><br>The first story, <b>Weaver of Dreams</b> features the Spider spinning her web and how and who gifted them with magic.<br><br>In the second one, <b>The Prince of Ebon Rih</b>, Lucivar is the main character, In this story, we learned how he met and fell in love with Marian, his wife.<br><br>The third one, <b>Zuulaman</b> is all about Saetan. Is narrated in the past. Saetan is still married to Hekatah and he has a son with her and another one on the way. In this one, you learn of the power Saetan has and how scheming and evil Heketah really is.<br><br>The fourth one, <b>Kaeleer’s Heart</b>, belongs to Daemon and Jaenelle. This short story happens after the events of the Queen of Darkness. A woman has decided that Daemon must be hers and she would do anything to get him. Mistakenly, she believes Daemon is staying with Jaenelle for duty and not love or attraction. Jaenelle is still recuperating and while weak, she is getting better day by day. She's just having trouble with any of the men around her to understanding that she's ready to<br><br>I like the last 3 stories. Weavers of Dreams is too short to offer an opinion.<br><br>I love romance, so Marion and Lucivar's love story was good with just the right amount of drama to enjoy it. I got to see another facet of Lucivar. One where he tries to be romantic but at the same time showing Marian how to defend herself instead of recurring to violence.<br><br>Zuulaman gave me a better understanding of the power of Saetan. It reinforced the love he had for his family and how when push comes to shove, he'll do whatever is necessary. <br><br>Jaenelle and Daemon's story wouldn't be as great without Surreal. She steals most of the scenes.<br><br>Overall, I liked it.<br><br>Cliffhanger: No<br><br>3.75/ 5 Fangs<br><br><a href="https://www.mrsleifs.com/2020/03/dreams-made-flesh-by-anne-bishop.html" rel="nofollow noopener">MrsLeif's Two Fangs About It</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/MrsLeifsbookreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/MrsLeifs_2Fangs" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/booksrmyworld/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_998041309" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/998041309" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/998041309?book_show_action=true">Nov 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6605429-dreams-made-flesh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer998041309" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8355091102865985069"><b>Dreams Made Flesh</b> is a collection of short stories and novellas set in the world of <b>Anne Bishop's</b> Black Jewel series, the stories add in some extra backstory and also work as an extended epilogue to the original trilogy so I wouldn't recommend reading this book until after <b>Queen of the Darkness</b>. If you enjoyed the first three books then I'm sure you'll love this collection though, it gives so much more insight into some of the character's backstories and I loved getting a chance to spend more ti</span>
  <span id="freeText8355091102865985069" style="display:none"><b>Dreams Made Flesh</b> is a collection of short stories and novellas set in the world of <b>Anne Bishop's</b> Black Jewel series, the stories add in some extra backstory and also work as an extended epilogue to the original trilogy so I wouldn't recommend reading this book until after <b>Queen of the Darkness</b>. If you enjoyed the first three books then I'm sure you'll love this collection though, it gives so much more insight into some of the character's backstories and I loved getting a chance to spend more time with some of my favourites.<br /><br />Let's talk about each story individually though to give you an idea what to expect:<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Weaver of Dreams:</u>
</b><br />This is set well before the beginning of the series and gives a bit more insight into the dream weaver spiders. The story is very short and I have to admit I didn't enjoy it as much as the others in this collection but it was interesting to read something from the point of view of a spider.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Prince of Ebon Rih:</u>
</b><br />In my opinion it would be worth buying this book for this story alone, I loved Lucivar's character in the original trilogy but even though I was glad that he had found a HEA I was disappointed we didn't get to see it happen for ourselves. This story fits into the timeline during <b>Queen of the Darkness</b> and lets us see how Lucivar and Marian first met and fell in love. They meet under dark circumstances but their actual romance was really sweet and heartwarming and I loved the way Marian stood up for Lucivar against an unwanted rival.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Zuulaman:</u>
</b><br />Another fab story this gives us a bit more background into the relationship between Saetan and Hekatah long before Daemon or Lucivar were born. This was pretty heartbreaking and made me love Saetan more than ever even though he takes truly drastic measures to get revenge after something horrendous happens. It never ceases to amaze me how low Hekatah is willing to sink in her quest for power but this shows us exactly why she's so terrified of Saetan throughout the series, he really isn't someone you should mess with!<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Kaeleer’s Heart:</u>
</b><br />This story is like an extended epilogue to <b>Queen of the Darkness</b> that shows us the fallout from Jaenelle's sacrifice both physically and emotionally. There's no denying what she did saved the world but the aftermath put a lot of strain on the relationship between Jaenelle and Daemon that they now need to work through in order to move forward. I really enjoyed seeing how Jaenelle was affected by what happened and how all of the family reacted to that. I also really liked how this story tied back in with <b>The Prince of Ebon Rih</b> with the reappearance of a certain character who desperately needed to get her comeuppance. I'll never get enough of this world or these characters so was thrilled with this glimpse into their happily ever after.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8355091102865985069" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_605911851" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/605911851" />
    <a title="Dianne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne"><img alt="Dianne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604666390p2/1401819.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/605911851?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dianne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dianne" href="/user/show/1401819-dianne">Dianne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6605429-dreams-made-flesh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401819-dianne?shelf=comfort-books">comfort-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401819-dianne?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401819-dianne?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401819-dianne?shelf=re-read">re-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1401819-dianne?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer605911851" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7777953766285106495">In my opinion, this book and most importantly the second story in it -"The Prince of Ebon Rih" needs to be read before you read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47959.Queen_of_the_Darkness__The_Black_Jewels___3_' title='Queen of the Darkness (The Black Jewels, #3) by Anne Bishop' rel='nofollow noopener'>Queen of the Darkness</a> . <br/><br/> The second story is my favorite and is about Lucivar finding the love of his life and coming out of his bleak shell. <br/><br/>The reason I find it so important to be read before Queen of the Darkness is that knowing Lucivars story will make the horror in QotD all that more realistic to the reader -and much more horrible for the horror fans!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14428216072902780516">This book contains 4 short stories set in the world of Anne Bishop's Black Jewels Trilogy and should only be read by those who have read at least the first 3 books. You don't need to read the 4th book as it has nothing to do with the events in this book. **Warning** If you haven't read the first 3 books there could be possible SPOILERS in this review. <br/><br/>The first story in Dreams Made Flesh is called "Weaver of Dreams" and my interpretaion is its about how the dream weaver spiders came to be. Out o</span>
  <span id="freeText14428216072902780516" style="display:none">This book contains 4 short stories set in the world of Anne Bishop's Black Jewels Trilogy and should only be read by those who have read at least the first 3 books. You don't need to read the 4th book as it has nothing to do with the events in this book. **Warning** If you haven't read the first 3 books there could be possible SPOILERS in this review. <br /><br />The first story in Dreams Made Flesh is called "Weaver of Dreams" and my interpretaion is its about how the dream weaver spiders came to be. Out of all the stories this one shortest and less interesting. A little because it was a tad confusing at what time this occured, before all of the Blood were created or at that start of when Jaenelle (Witch) was made into existence.It was beautifully written with very dark descriptions but I was a tad confused of the timeline. <br />"The Prince of Ebon Rih", is about how Lucivar and Marianne met, I enjoyed finding out about the progression of this relationship. <br />"Zuulaman", the third story, for me this was an awesome story, but I am a bit confused as to <br />why, if Saetan has such power,why he couldnt use it to destroy Dorothea and get his sons back. However he does have an awesome power and I liked reading more about him. <br />The fourth and last story is "Kaeleers Heart", and is about the events that occured between Jaenelle and Daemon after Book #3 in the trilogy, for those of you who wanted more closure after that book this one ties up a few loose ends. I must confess I am getting quite bored with Jaenelle and Daemons relationship problems. But if you are a big fan of those two you will love this story too. <br /><br />Bottom line this was a good "fix" for my Anne Bishop addiction but I am wearing thin on the Jaenelle/Daemon relationship. They were more fun when <br />in the earlier books</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3179045074" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14604160320791490428"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>I've enjoyed the dark and intriguing world of <i>The Black Jewels</i>. <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> consists of four stories that gives more insight and depth to the world building and it's characters.<br/><br/><b>Weaver of Dreams :</b> This was too short to form any opinion but it was intriguing how much power and dreams were woven into the web for The Witch. <br/><br/><b>The Prince of Ebon Rih:</b> In <i>Queen of Darkness</i> Lucivar was already married to Marian. This story gives the background of how it happened. It's the best in this colle</span>
  <span id="freeText14604160320791490428" style="display:none"><b>3.5 Stars</b><br /><br />I've enjoyed the dark and intriguing world of <i>The Black Jewels</i>. <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> consists of four stories that gives more insight and depth to the world building and it's characters.<br /><br /><b>Weaver of Dreams :</b> This was too short to form any opinion but it was intriguing how much power and dreams were woven into the web for The Witch. <br /><br /><b>The Prince of Ebon Rih:</b> In <i>Queen of Darkness</i> Lucivar was already married to Marian. This story gives the background of how it happened. It's the best in this collection. <br /><br /><b>Zuulaman:</b> Saetan has always been portrayed as a loving and caring father figure to Jaenelle and the coven. In Zuulaman we get to see his ruthless side. Saetan has been my favorite character and to see him interacting with Peyton and Mephis, making mistakes and wielding so much power was a pleasure to read. I thought I couldn't hate Heketah more but this proved me wrong. <br /><br /><b>Kaeleer’s Heart:</b> The ending of <i>Queen of Darkness</i> had left me unsatisfied. This story picked up right off the events that led to Jaenelle's sacrifice and it's aftermath. It was fun to see Daemon and Jaenelle working on their relationship but after sometimes it got boring. I thought the story was dragged a bit with all unnecessary drama from another witch. <br /><br />All in all <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> is an interesting addition to this series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14604160320791490428" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13319776934917041077">The short stories in this book are best read only if you read the original Black Jewels Trilogy as they fill in some of the blanks. I must say these stories are a lot less gritty and dark than the trilogy (except for one), but I found three of them a joy to read and was happy to find out more about some of the things that were only hinted at in the trilogy. Bishop's writing is excellent and rich as always.<br/><br/>Here's an overview of the stories:<br/><br/>Weaver of Dreams<br/>This story is about the creation of the J</span>
  <span id="freeText13319776934917041077" style="display:none">The short stories in this book are best read only if you read the original Black Jewels Trilogy as they fill in some of the blanks. I must say these stories are a lot less gritty and dark than the trilogy (except for one), but I found three of them a joy to read and was happy to find out more about some of the things that were only hinted at in the trilogy. Bishop's writing is excellent and rich as always.<br /><br />Here's an overview of the stories:<br /><br />Weaver of Dreams<br />This story is about the creation of the Jewels and although I loved the richly written text I found the story a bit boring I must confess.<br /><br />The Prince of Ebon Rih<br />This story is about how Lucivar finds love. <br />I really like this one and was glad it was included as I thought Lucivar's marriage was glossed over very hastily in the Trilogy.<br /><br />Zuulaman<br />This is the only dark and disturbing story of the four, but I loved it. It gives more insight in Saetan and why he became who and what he is.<br /><br />Kaeleer's Heart<br />This is the story about what happens just after the end of the original Trilogy and centers on Jaenelle and Daemon. A great read.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2906510824810830126" style="display:none">"You are my breath, my life, my heart."<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1521176547i/25221101._SX540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The is a quartet of stories from the world of the Black Jewels.<br><br>1. Zuuluman - a glimpse into Saetan's history. What happened to his third child is so sad and awful, but this outcome I more Sadist than the High Lord we've seen, so it was definitely interesting.<br><br>4. Kaeleer's Heart - what happens to Jaenelle and Daemon after the ending of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/47959.Queen_of_the_Darkness__The_Black_Jewels___3_" title="Queen of the Darkness (The Black Jewels, #3) by Anne Bishop" rel="nofollow noopener">Queen of the Darkness</a>. <div id="review_2665067365" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2665067365" />
    <a title="Kathy Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin"><img alt="Kathy Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1459738550p2/3122948.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2665067365?book_show_action=true">Jan 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathy Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathy Martin" href="/user/show/3122948-kathy-martin">Kathy Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2665067365" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11037861356782555622">This anthology contains four stories set in the Black Jewels universe.<br/><br/>Weaver of Dreams tells how spiders learned from a dying dragon how to weave webs that can hold or create lives.<br/><br/>The Prince of Ebon Rih takes place after the events of Heir to the Shadows and tells the story of Lucivar's courtship of Marian.<br/><br/>Zuulaman tells a story from Saetan's past when he was married to Hekatah and the Warlord Prince of Dhemlan. A country called Zuulaman tries to get the best of his country, aided by the 100 fa</span>
  <span id="freeText11037861356782555622" style="display:none">This anthology contains four stories set in the Black Jewels universe.<br /><br />Weaver of Dreams tells how spiders learned from a dying dragon how to weave webs that can hold or create lives.<br /><br />The Prince of Ebon Rih takes place after the events of Heir to the Shadows and tells the story of Lucivar's courtship of Marian.<br /><br />Zuulaman tells a story from Saetan's past when he was married to Hekatah and the Warlord Prince of Dhemlan. A country called Zuulaman tries to get the best of his country, aided by the 100 families of Hyall and Hekatah, and Saetan shows them just what a black-jeweled warlord prince can do.<br /><br />Kaeleer's Heart tells what happens after the events of Queen of the Darkness when Jaenelle heals quite changed and Daemon wonders if she doesn't love him anymore. Their relationship is complicated by someone who wants to ruin Daemon's reputation and wreck his relationship with Jaenelle so that he will turn to her. He shows everyone why he was nicknamed the Sadist while he was a pleasure slave in Terreille. <br /><br />All of these stories were great at providing more about the fascinating Black Jewels world. The Prince of Ebon Rih and Kaeleer's Heart were also wonderful romances.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11037861356782555622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1302043848" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1302043848" />
    <a title="Kerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/382536-kerry"><img alt="Kerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1241083653p2/382536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1302043848?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry" href="/user/show/382536-kerry">Kerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=10">10</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=reread">reread</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=2007">2007</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/382536-kerry?shelf=rereads-in-2018">rereads-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1302043848" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9208050921530312647">REREAD #1: "Kaeleer's Heart" 15 September 2018 - 16 September 2018 (10/10)<br/><br/>A little while back, a friend and I were watching the 1982 film adaption of <i>The Scarlet Pimpernel</i> and at one point I was shouting at the screen in frustration "Just talk to each other!" The big misunderstanding that could be solved with a bit of conversation is a major trope in romances and I'm too old for it these days. I just want to lock the couple in question in a room and not let them out until they talk. That made me</span>
  <span id="freeText9208050921530312647" style="display:none">REREAD #1: "Kaeleer's Heart" 15 September 2018 - 16 September 2018 (10/10)<br /><br />A little while back, a friend and I were watching the 1982 film adaption of <i>The Scarlet Pimpernel</i> and at one point I was shouting at the screen in frustration "Just talk to each other!" The big misunderstanding that could be solved with a bit of conversation is a major trope in romances and I'm too old for it these days. I just want to lock the couple in question in a room and not let them out until they talk. That made me comment that I loved the final story in this book, "Kaeleer's Heart" that plays with this trope in a way that makes me very, very happy.<br /><br />A week or so after that conversation, my husband and I managed to fit a couple more bookshelves into our small house and I was able to move some of my books out of storage and into the house. Of course, all my Black Jewels books were among those I chose. So when I couldn't decide what to read last night, I remembered my idea to reread this story and happily pulled the book off the shelf to do so. It is still as awesome and wonderful as before and I am now fighting the urge to reread all nine books.<br /><br />If you want my thoughts, read down to my previous review. I still feel the same way.<br /><br /><br />FIRST READ: Finished 4 June, 2007 (10/10)<br /><br /><em>Blurb:</em><br />Set in the realm of The Black Jewels trilogy, this collection features four brand-new revelatory stories of Jaenelle and her kindred.<br /><br /><em>My Comments:</em><br />Anne Bishop continues to impress. This book contains four short stories from the past and future of the Black Jewels Realms and I love them all, but especially the ones about Lucivar and Marian and about Jaenelle and Daemon.<br /><br />The first is a very short piece about how the golden spiders gained sentience and power.<br /><br />The second tells the story of Lucivar and Marian's courtship. Here, Bishop shows she can take a standard romance outline and tell a magical tale. Many a romance author could read this to find out exactly how to write an alpha male and make a success of it. A brilliant success.<br /><br />The third tells of a black moment in Saetan's life and explains why he never tried to keep Lucivar and Daemon when they were taken from them. We learn that he control of his power and temper was hard won and have part of the answer to the question of who would win if Saetan and Daemon ever faced off.<br /><br />The fourth story takes up where "Queen of the Darkness" left off, telling the tale of how Jaenelle and Daemon reconnect as Jaenelle heals. As these two were my favourites in the main series, this was a total delight. Again, Bishop has taken a romance trope and shown how it should be done in this beautiful fantasy story.<br /><br />Someone is trying to sew discord between Daemon and Jaenelle and they need all their combined strength as they combat this new enemy and come to terms with the changes in Jaenelle due to her actions in "Queen of the Darkness". As some who reads some romance (and reads <i>about</i> it more) this story is a triumph where the characters, facing misunderstanding and confusion sown by their enemy and their own actions, actually <i>talk</i> to each other and resolve the problem instead of letting it fester for hundreds of pages. Congratulations to Anne Bishop, Jaenelle and Daemon.<br /><br />This story shows also shows us fundamental differences between Daemon and Jaenelle and how they compliment each other. Jaenelle does all the things she does because she loves and cares about the people around her. She stays in Challiot for Whilemena, she forms the Dark Court to save the Kindred, she does everything she does to save the Blood. Daemon on the other hand, does the things he does solely for Jaenelle. She is his concern. His to protect and cherish. If he cares about others (and he does) and what they think of him, it takes a distant backseat to what Jaenelle needs of and from him.<br /><br />This story also provides the rest of what is needed to answer that question of who would win a confrontation between Daemon and Saetan. Especially if it concerned Jaenelle, it would be Daemon. Saetan rightly fears his power and has a rigid control; Daemon will simply use his without any such consideration.<br /><br />I have rapidly become and Anne Bishop fangirl and will happily shout her praises to the rooftops. I am not generally a short story reader, but I do love them when the further my knowledge and understanding of people and places I don't want to leave behind yet. That is exactly what "Dreams Made Flesh" does and it was a welcome addition to the tales of the Blood.<br /><br />[Copied from LibraryThing.]</span>
  <a data-text-id="9208050921530312647" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1751064682" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1751064682" />
    <a title="Darkphoenix" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7928371-darkphoenix"><img alt="Darkphoenix" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1341503672p2/7928371.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1751064682?book_show_action=true">Sep 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Darkphoenix" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Darkphoenix" href="/user/show/7928371-darkphoenix">Darkphoenix</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1751064682" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8570930406264847052">I loved the first three books and I loved the characters and I liked the way that arc ended. The trouble with Dreams Made Flesh is that ideally it should have focused on secondary characters, like the other queens instead of sticking with Jaenelle and Daemon. Allow me to explain.<br/><br/>I liked the first story about the creation of the Web of Dreams, it was interesting, like an origin story. Then there was the second story about the courtship of Lucivar and Marian and even that was enjoyable. But in tha</span>
  <span id="freeText8570930406264847052" style="display:none">I loved the first three books and I loved the characters and I liked the way that arc ended. The trouble with Dreams Made Flesh is that ideally it should have focused on secondary characters, like the other queens instead of sticking with Jaenelle and Daemon. Allow me to explain.<br /><br />I liked the first story about the creation of the Web of Dreams, it was interesting, like an origin story. Then there was the second story about the courtship of Lucivar and Marian and even that was enjoyable. But in that story, we met Luthvian and Roxie yet again. Luthvian may have redeemed herself at the end of Queen of the Darkness but here she was far from that version of herself. She was hateful and manipulative.<br /><br />I liked Lucivar and Marian. They were a sweet pair and I liked that Marian wasn't afraid of letting Lucivar know when he was behaving like a neanderthal. For his part, Lucivar tried to be patient and mostly succeeded. And perhaps, most of all I enjoyed their interactions with Jaenelle (the first time she, Marian and Saetan go shopping was hilarious) But then the irritants started piling on. I've already mentioned Luthvian. Then there was Roxie. She is so vile, like a disgusting insect, except even they serve some purpose. She was just vile and I couldn't understand why Luthvian let her stay with her when she knew that she made her son uncomfortable. She knew what Lucivar had gone through in Terielle and she still let Roxie parade around him. Here she was even more outrageous, letting people think that not only was Lucivar sleeping with her but when that didn't work, she planned to accuse him of rape and let him wear the Ring of Obedience. Thankfully that didn't happen thanks to Marian.<br /><br />I didn't read the story about Hekatah making Saetan's life miserable, I had seen enough of her in the first three books and I had no intention of reading more about her. The final story is about Daemon trying to help Jaenelle after the events of the Queen of the Darkness. She lost her dark Jewels but gained a new one, the Twilight's Dusk. In addition to seeing Daemon try to reach Jaenelle and rekindle their relationship, there was also the additional (and unnecessary plot) of another aristo woman, Lektra trying to lure Daemon to her bed.<br /><br />She spreads rumors of his infidelity and when that doesn't work, she tries to sabotage the carriage that Daemon and Jaenelle were in and when even that backfires, she decides to insinuate to Daemon that Jaenelle had taken another lover. I mean seriously! Give me a break. Haven't we already dealt with women like that? And of course, once again Roxie was back. Why wasn't she dead? I thought all the Blood who had Dorothea and Hekatah's taint had perished. If anyone in the Dhemlan had their taint, it was Roxie so why was she still alive. So she's also back stirring trouble.<br /><br />While it was fun seeing more of Jaenelle, Daemon, Lucivar and Surreal, that joy was undermined by the sheer frustration with regard to the plot. I'll admit, I wasn't very worried that the women's hair-brained schemes would work just because by now, the reader has a very clear idea about just how deep Daemon's devotion to Jaenelle is and that he genuinely loves her. Having said that, it was gratifying to see the women get what they deserve. They tangled with the Sadist and had no idea what they were getting themselves into.<br /><br />The frustration stems from the fact that the plot feels repetitive. We've seen these themes before and not much has changed here. It was engrossing the first time but then it got dragged for three whole books. In Dreams Made Flesh (and in the final story to be precise) the plot just feels old. There was nothing new here, nothing exciting. Which is why I said that it would have been better to focus on secondary characters instead of going back to the original protagonists time and again. Their story concluded and concluded well, let them be. I would have liked to see Karla (one of my favourite characters from the first three books) or Gabrielle or some of the other Queens. But far from focusing on them, they didn't even appear.<br /><br />I'm going to give these books a break now, if at all, I'll read Tangled Web but not anytime soon. I think I'm done with this universe and I want to leave while I still like the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8570930406264847052" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer3768952244703975396">I have never read a book in The Black Jewels series. I've tried and everytime I open that first book I get irritated. The style doesn't work for me, the characters seem ugh, and yet. I adore this book. <br/><br/>I really do. It makes no sense but there you have it. My least favourite is the opening story. I get that that might be because I haven't read the series but it was a bit confusing and while I appreciate the way she wrote it from a different POV, and we were as confused as the spider at first, it </span>
  <span id="freeText3768952244703975396" style="display:none">I have never read a book in The Black Jewels series. I've tried and everytime I open that first book I get irritated. The style doesn't work for me, the characters seem ugh, and yet. I adore this book. <br /><br />I really do. It makes no sense but there you have it. My least favourite is the opening story. I get that that might be because I haven't read the series but it was a bit confusing and while I appreciate the way she wrote it from a different POV, and we were as confused as the spider at first, it still felt like a bit much but at the same time, not enough. <br /><br />The second story is my favourite, hands down. I love Saetan if only because of the way he is as a person is so at odds with who you'd think he'd be because of his position. I love that Lucivar is still pained by the things done to him in his past and yet he doesn't hate all women because of it. And him wooing Marian was so sweet. I love that she was still shy and sweet but had her moments without it seeming forced or taking away from her character. <br /><br />Zuulaman is my second favourite just because it shows a side of Saetan you don't see in the first short story and even while I'm thinking about what was done, at the same time, my heart is breaking for him because no one seems to quite grasp the pain he's feeling as well as the way it has to hurt to have everyone treat him like a monster. I'm unsure as to why someone that powerful couldn't just end his bitch wives and WHY he only seems to have bitch wives since he seems like an intelligent and kind human being but I guess that's what happens when you skip books, lol. <br /><br />The last one wasn't a fave. It was alright. But then again, a main problem I have with the series is Jaenelle so that could be what diminished this for me because it was wonderfully written and I like how we opened with one brother and closed with the other and while there were similarities you could see how they are so different as well. <br /><br />A great book and I'd say I'd try the trilogy again because of this book, but in reality the concept of the actual series fails for me, but this just hit all the right buttons. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125104159" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11869486080446354404">I honestly don't know how many times I re-read <u>Dreams Made Flesh</u> a collection of stories from the Black Jewels trilogy, but each and every time I find something new that I love about Anne Bishop's strangely dark and compelling world. Truthfully though, I just fall head over heels in love with those delicious SaDiablo/Yaslana males all over again. I know, I know, but every time Daemon Sadi croons about "dancing with The Sadist", I just want to. I love Bishop's take on alpha males. The SaDiablo/Ya</span>
  <span id="freeText11869486080446354404" style="display:none">I honestly don't know how many times I re-read <u>Dreams Made Flesh</u> a collection of stories from the Black Jewels trilogy, but each and every time I find something new that I love about Anne Bishop's strangely dark and compelling world. Truthfully though, I just fall head over heels in love with those delicious SaDiablo/Yaslana males all over again. I know, I know, but every time Daemon Sadi croons about "dancing with The Sadist", I just want to. I love Bishop's take on alpha males. The SaDiablo/Yaslana men--Saetan, Daemon and Lucivar--are extremly virile and powerful men. They can be both tender and violent, and yet they surrender that power to the Witch they serve and the women they love, and woe unto anyone who gets in their way. In fact, I just love the way Bishop's matriarchal society works. It's not perfect. Bad Queens can rule and the men who serve them can be corrupted.<br /><br />One line in particular between Lucivar and Jaenelle illustrates that dynamic very well: <i>He didn't want her sexually--had never wanted her that way--but the hugs and sisterly kisses kept him balanced in a way nothing else had ever done. 'Hold the leash', he silently pleaded. 'Choke me into obedience if that's what it takes.'</i> <br /><br />To fans of the BDB or any of those other so-called "alphas"--can you imagine any of THOSE guys willing to be that strong in their vulnerability? Short answer: Not Bloody Likely!!!<br /> <br />There are four stories within this collection: <u>Weaver of Dreams</u>, which is about the origin of the jewels and of the Blood who are the guardians of the realms. <u>The Prince of Ebon Rih</u>, is my favorite story about Lucivar Yaslana, the winged Eyrien Warlord Prince who falls in love with Mirian, a quiet but strong-willed hearth witch. <u>Zuulaman</u> is the story of what one man does when driven to the brink of sanity by an unspeakable act. <u>Kaleer's Heart</u> brings back Jaenelle and Daemon at a crossroads in their fragile relationship as another witch schemes to steal him away. Not a very wise thing to do...tangling with The Sadist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11869486080446354404" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Kerry (The Roaming Librarian) O&#39;Donnell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry (The Roaming Librarian) O&#39;Donnell" href="/user/show/195463-kerry-the-roaming-librarian-o-donnell">Kerry (The Roaming Librarian) O&#39;Donnell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780451460134" href="/book/show/480797.Dreams_Made_Flesh">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/195463-kerry-the-roaming-librarian-o-donnell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/195463-kerry-the-roaming-librarian-o-donnell?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3130569" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11811255572858432655">Every time I read these short stories, I feel like I'm getting together with good friends. Sounds kinda weird probably, but I've read the stories set in the Black Jewels Realms more times than I can remember. Yet each time, new parts, places, and dialogue will stand out in a way it didn't before. This time around I found myself really enjoying the language Bishop uses, and the brilliant way that she crafts sentences. <br/><br/>As far as the stories themselves, I think they definitely mean more if you're a</span>
  <span id="freeText11811255572858432655" style="display:none">Every time I read these short stories, I feel like I'm getting together with good friends. Sounds kinda weird probably, but I've read the stories set in the Black Jewels Realms more times than I can remember. Yet each time, new parts, places, and dialogue will stand out in a way it didn't before. This time around I found myself really enjoying the language Bishop uses, and the brilliant way that she crafts sentences. <br /><br />As far as the stories themselves, I think they definitely mean more if you're already familiar with the original trilogy. Bishop doesn't waste too much time (or too many pages) on past events, but her characters are clearly affected by them and in certain stories are reacting to things that happened within that original set. Someone who doesn't know them could get confused, but more likely, they will get curious as to what happened and why. Another thing to mention is these stories take place at varying times; two happen before the initial setting of the books, one is set in the middle of the trilogy but was originally glossed over, and one more that takes place after the original stories concluded.<br /><br />I suppose I should also admit that my favorite story out of the four is <i>The Prince of Ebon Rih</i>. Without spoiling anything let me just say that it focuses on Lucivar Yaslana, who is one of my two favorite characters of all the novels of the Black Jewels series and as such, that's why its my favorite. He's just such a fun character to read about! Though if I had to pick, I would want to be Surreal SaDiablo (my other favorite). She doesn't feature quite as much in this collection, but boy does she make her presence known on the page. <br /><br />Okay, now I'm done before I get all giddy and fangirl-y. Happy reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11811255572858432655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20826582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6228009634181681163">I absolutely loooooved this book. <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> is an anthology of short stories surrounding the <i>Black Jewels Trilogy</i>, focusing on the aftermath and the past, as well as giving a greater insight into the lesser characters. <br/><br/>I must admit, I was most determined to read this book for <i>Kaeleer's Heart</i>, the story of Jaenelle and Daemon. I found their love to be absolutely beautiful in the trilogy and I wanted moremoremore of it. As much as possible. <br/><br/>However, I finished this book with so much more t</span>
  <span id="freeText6228009634181681163" style="display:none">I absolutely loooooved this book. <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> is an anthology of short stories surrounding the <i>Black Jewels Trilogy</i>, focusing on the aftermath and the past, as well as giving a greater insight into the lesser characters. <br /><br />I must admit, I was most determined to read this book for <i>Kaeleer's Heart</i>, the story of Jaenelle and Daemon. I found their love to be absolutely beautiful in the trilogy and I wanted moremoremore of it. As much as possible. <br /><br />However, I finished this book with so much more to fall in love with. For example, <i>The Prince of Ebon Rih</i>. Reading the trilogy, I did not think much of Marian. She was just... there. That woman who had captured Lucivar's heart. To be honest, I sort of resented her. She hadn't been given a proper introduction into Queen of Darkness, it was just that all of a sudden, between Heir to the Shadows and Queen of the Darkness, she'd arrived. That's it. But this story gave us an insight into her character as well as Lucivar, and I've found myself loving this couple as much as, if not MORE than, Daemon and Jaenelle. I have so much respect for Marian, she's definitely one of my favourite characters now.<br /><br />But why am I giving this book five stars? Why, for <b>ZUULAMAN</b>. This short story was ABSOLUTELY FANTASTIC! I was in complete and utter AWE reading Zuulaman, it was just so amazing. The stunning conclusion just tears your breath away, and it really gives a depth to Saetan (and to Daemon, for that matter) that we never received in the trilogy. Even Hekatah, who I'd completely underestimated until reading this. Really, I GUSHED OVER THIS STORY FOR AGES. If anything, <i>Dreams Made Flesh</i> is worth reading for <b>Zuulaman</b>. &lt;3</span>
  <a data-text-id="6228009634181681163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('wQOxGCiOodFTtfWlZcK1Fmb90QSYB7LVgryoCxmG8ghY0ucXc7VLcUY8LDmsu/e/rkxacApCaDybQHk/aM690A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<span id="freeTextContainer2300470589061796910">Anne Bishop lives in upstate New York where she enjoys gardening, music, and writing dark, romantic stories. She is the author of over twenty novels, including the award-winning Black Jewels Trilogy. Why would I care about what you looked like? The flesh was the shell that housed the glory[....] Even if I couldn't be your physical lover, there are other ways to be a lover and I know them all. So don't stand there and tell me how you feel depends on <i>how you look!</i>&rdquo;</span>
